I'm sure this won't be the last word in this thread, but it might be the last word on "The Last Word" (from dictionary.com):

What is the absolute last word in any dictionary?

Zyxt is listed as the last word in the online Oxford English Dictionary, an obsolete Kentish word that is the second singular indicative present form of the verb see. The next-to-last is zyxst, an obsolete word meaning 'sixth'. Several online dictionaries list the word zyzzyva, a tropical American weevil, as the last word in the letter Z.

Hmm, actually, I suppose the next logical question is what's the absolute last word in any dictionary IN ANY LANGUAGE!

First of all, U B da girlie. Not moi.

Secondly, it doesn't matter if they are bigger than 128 KB. You are simply referring to them. (BTW, this doesn't work with stuff you've uploaded from your cellphone.) THIS IS FOR BUDDY AND MACINTOSH USERS ONLY.

Search anywhere on the world wide internetz to find a picture you want to use. "Control + Click" on the photo; a menu will open; click on "Open Image In New Tab; highlight the URL of the isolated image and "Command + C" (cut) the URL; then place that URL into the box at the bottom of each page in JHL where it says Quick Reply; click preview; when the preview comes up, highlight what you have inserted in the box and click on the image icon above the box.

Now you too can do this!

Title: Re: The Last Word!
Post by: foobah on April 08, 2008, 01:25:54 PM
BTW, if anybody's curious what my leader board program looks like, here it is:

Code: [Select]
#!perl
use strict;
use Time::Local;
use LWP::UserAgent;
use HTTP::Request::Common qw(GET POST);

my %months = (January => 0, February => 1, March => 2,
      April => 3, May => 4, June => 5,
      July => 6, August => 7, September => 8,
      October => 9, November => 10, December => 11);

my $ua = LWP::UserAgent->new();

my $postNo = 0;
my $page = $ua->request(GET "http://www.jacksonheightslife.com/community/index.php?topic=648.$postNo");
my($lastPage) = $page->content =~ /Pages:.*<a.*?href=".*topic=648\.(\d+)/;

my(%lastWord, %numPosts);
my($lastFrom, $lastTime);

POSTS:
my @posts = $page->content =~ /(<tr>(?:.(?!<\/tr>))*?View the profile of.*?<\/tr>)/gs;

foreach my $post (@posts) {
  my($from)     = $post =~ /View the profile of ([^"]+)/;
  my($datetime) = $post =~ /on:<\/b> (.*?) &/;

  my($month, $day, $year, $hour, $min, $sec, $ampm);
  if ($datetime =~ /<b>(Yesterday|Today)<\/b> at (\d{2}):(\d{2}):(\d{2}) (\w{2})/) {
    ($hour, $min, $sec, $ampm) = ($2, $3, $4, $5);
    if ($1 eq 'Today') {
      ($day, $month, $year) = (localtime)[3, 4, 5];
    } else {
      ($day, $month, $year) = (localtime(time - 86_400))[3, 4, 5];
    }
  } else {
    ($month, $day, $year, $hour, $min, $sec, $ampm) = $datetime =~ /(\w+) (\d{2}), (\d{4}), (\d{2}):(\d{2}):(\d{2}) (\w{2})/;
    $year -= 1900;
    $month = $months{$month};
  }

  if ($hour == 12) {
    if ($ampm eq 'AM') {
      $hour = 0;
    }
  } else {
    if ($ampm eq 'PM') {
      $hour += 12;
    }
  }

  my $time = timelocal($sec, $min, $hour, $day, $month, $year);
  if (not defined $lastFrom) {
    $lastFrom = $from;
    $lastTime = $time;
  } else {
    $lastWord{$lastFrom} += ($time - $lastTime);
    $lastFrom = $from;
    $lastTime = $time;
  }

  $numPosts{$from}++;
}

if ($postNo < $lastPage) {
  $postNo += 15;
  $page = $ua->request(GET "http://www.jacksonheightslife.com/community/index.php?topic=648.$postNo");
  goto POSTS;
}

$lastWord{$lastFrom} += (time - $lastTime);

print "[u]TLW Leader Board as of " . localtime() . "[/u]\n";

foreach my $from (sort { $lastWord{$b} <=> $lastWord{$a} } keys %lastWord) {
  my $time = $lastWord{$from};

  my $days = sprintf "%d", $time / 86_400; $time -= $days * 86_400;
  my $hours = sprintf "%d", $time / 3600;  $time -= $hours * 3600;
  my $minutes = sprintf "%d", $time / 60;  $time -= $minutes * 60;
  my $seconds = sprintf "%d", $time;

  my $dayLabel = $days == 1 ? 'day' : 'days';
  my $houLabel = $hours == 1 ? 'hour' : 'hours';
  my $minLabel = $minutes == 1 ? 'minute' : 'minutes';
  my $secLabel = $seconds == 1 ? 'second' : 'seconds';
  my $posLabel = $numPosts{$from} == 1 ? 'post' : 'posts';

  print "$from: $numPosts{$from} $posLabel, last word for $days $dayLabel, $hours $houLabel, $minutes $minLabel and $seconds $secLabel\n";
}

Title: Re: The Last Word!

Actually, according to Godwin's Law as originally posted by michaelb, this argument was over when NYCMac posted the photo of Hilter.  Mac, you have the official last word on this thread! :2funny:

Quote from: michaelb on April 08, 2008, 12:18:24 AM
Godwin's law is a tradition that has lasted since the early 90s.

Excerpt from the Wikipedia article (http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Godwin%27s_Law):

Godwin's Law (also known as Godwin's Rule of Nazi Analogies)[1] is an adage formulated by Mike Godwin in 1990. The law states:

    "As a Usenet discussion grows longer, the probability of a comparison involving Nazis or Hitler approaches one."

Godwin's Law is often cited in online discussions as a caution against the use of inflammatory rhetoric or exaggerated comparisons, and is often conflated with fallacious arguments of the reductio ad Hitlerum form.

The rule does not make any statement whether any particular reference or comparison to Hitler or the Nazis might be appropriate, but only asserts that one arising is increasingly probable. It is precisely because such a comparison or reference may sometimes be appropriate, Godwin has argued that overuse of Nazi and Hitler comparisons should be avoided, because it robs the valid comparisons of their impact. Although in one of its early forms Godwin's Law referred specifically to Usenet newsgroup discussions, the law is now applied to any threaded online discussion: electronic mailing lists, message boards, chat rooms, and more recently blog comment threads and wiki talk pages.

'Allo everyone!

Been busy outside in the sun and cleaning up from the recent construction work.

Might stay up to try to have LW for the day. Might crash.

Gardening yesterday. Sooo good for the spirit! We made a little pathway with reclaimed bricks. No money involved, just spirit and sweat.
The chives, lemon thyme, parsley, lemon balm, oregano, pineapple mint, valerian (looks good, not useful) and worm wood all survived. We think the tarragon did, too, and maybe the lavender.

Strawberries have blossoms on them.

Basil planting and different kind thyme in the the near future.

Yay, Spring!

PS The garden is public, over at Saint Mark's on the 82nd St. side, to the left of the door. Feel free to pick herbs judiciously, or, better, come and dig with us!

Title: Re: The Last Word!
Post by: ECG on May 09, 2008, 11:44:47 PM
Apologies to all. Yes, the Louis Armstrong house. I loved the kitchen and all the wallpaper.

Sump pump - well, many years ago, shortly after Thanksgiving, my son and I were awoken by a geyser of water shooting up out of the kitchen sink! It was raining out and whatever the problem with the building's aging water lines and downspouts had caused a mini Old Faithful.

After hours of bailing, disinfecting, etc. We blocked the drain, put a heavy kettle with rocks in it over the drain and had the plumber come.

The son is a very cautious person and went out and purchased a sump pump in case it happened again. It hasn't, but there are very strange sounds from that sink still.

It was an awful experience and we still had to go to work in the morning. Ugh.


Title: Re: The Last Word!
Post by: NYCMacUser on May 10, 2008, 05:34:38 AM
My Mom and (Aunt) Lucy, (Uncle) Satchmo's wife, had a weekly poker game that rotated from house to house. Although I was only around 7 and my sister around 10, I vividly remember the night my Dad was out of town and Mom took us to the game at their house. (Uncle) Satchmo played games with us and then he and 2 of his friends took us out for dinner to a restaurant on either Northern or Queens Boulevard for fried chicken and French fries. (I wish I could remember the name of the place.) I didn't realize the significance of this until many, many years later when I heard him retell the story at my wedding about how 3 black men took 2 little, red-haired, white girls out for fried chicken at a family-style restaurant and how they were at first unwilling to seat us until they realized who he was. Whenever that poker game was at our house, Aunt Lucy always brought my sister and me a board game to keep us busy so the cussing-related game could be played without interruption.

The Armstrongs will always have a very special place in my heart for the kindnesses and love they shared with us. My darling Aunt Lucy especially, for all those forbidden words we learned on Tuesday nights.
Title: Re: The Last Word!
Post by: ECG on May 10, 2008, 05:01:03 PM
Oh, Mac, what a NICE story! Thank you for sharing it.

I didn't know the Armstrongs at all, but once held the door for Mrs. A when she was going into Clark's. Later my mom told me who she was. I was really thrilled.

One of the goals of my life is to be as wonderful as those 'grown ups' I admired as a child. It's so hard to tell if you are making any kind of positive difference in this era and I'm pretty discouraged right now.

I am friends with the grand daughter of my 'Auntie Mame'. This woman would let me stay over at her house when my uncle and 4 horrible cousins* would come to stay, she took me to the theater and out to posh restaurants, and was one of the wittiest people I've ever known.

Fortunately the grand daughter has inherited the wit, and I am thrilled that, even though I'm 20 years older than she, we are equals and friends.

Great First Words of the Day, Mac!


*once they grew up, they were okay.

Title: Re: The Last Word!
Post by: NYC Native on June 08, 2008, 08:49:56 AM
Quote from: buddy on June 06, 2008, 09:00:38 PM
okay, I'll bite.  I know what salsa is but what is bachata?????  And I'm having my merlot right now.   ;)

Bachata is a type of music that was considered to be sort of "lowly" by many Dominicans because it was usually heard in the "bayus" or lowly bars of the "barrios" of the DR.  Themes usually touched the subject of relations gone bad...heck, we used to call it "musica de cuernos"  :2funny:   But since it was mostly the Dominicans that came from many of these barrios they also imported the music and for a while in the 90's it was really popular among their community.  Still is among the Dominicans and many of the Central Americans.  The music became more refined as more capable musicians started to record  bachata  (just as the case of merengue).  The dance is only 3 or 4 steps but it's simplicity (not unlike merengue) makes it a popular type of dance and music among the smaller queens clubs and many in the Heights.

On my way to the parade!!!(http://img11.glitterfy.com/graphics/42/puerto_rico.gif)

Title: Re: The Last Word!
Post by: NYCMacUser on June 16, 2008, 04:41:04 PM
Quote from: buddy on June 16, 2008, 02:31:00 AM
Do they have snow in July in South American?  I DON'T THINK SO but I've never been.

How was the BBQ?
Bariloche, Argentina
Las Lenas, Argentina
Portillo, Chile
Termas De Chillan, Chile
Valle Nevado, Chile

Not cheap, mind you. There are also resorts in Colombia, Ecuador, Peru and Bolivia. But the luxury ones are all in Argentina and Chile as is the best powder. The season is from June to around the end of September the first week of October. But if you can imagine boarding a plane at JFK in 103 degree weather in the middle of August, and disembarking in frigid weather and heading for the slopes . . . I DID IT IN 1988. It was number 26 on my Bucket List. Thank G-d, I was religious about doing one from my list (which I started in Junior High School) every couple of years.

The BBQ was such fun. Doggies, doggies everywhere! Well behaved doggies, too, that is until the boomers started! We all got soaked, well-fed, duly inebriated and ended up with sore jaws from all the laughing. There was enough food for a small invading army; hamburgers, Kosher hot dogs, Italian sausage, marinated chicken breasts, dried lamb lung, salads, Key Lime pies, ice cream sammies with whipped cream and cherries, soft drinks, hard drinks, beer, and, of course, all the fixins! Oh, yeah, the dried lamb lungs were exclusively for the doggies.

FELICES PASCUAS

(http://www.alamedainfo.com/Expo_67_United_Nations_Pavilion_PC_002.jpg)
There was this Italian guy...an artist, a singer and poet.  went to Puerto Rico for a vacation and ended up moving there.  He made Friends with the local artist and became very interested in the "musica del campo".  He loved it, reminded him of when he was a child, he said.  He is gone now...but his music is still here...specially during "las Navidades"

Title: Re: The Last Word!
Post by: NYC Native on May 01, 2009, 12:01:35 PM
Quote from: Shelby2 on April 30, 2009, 11:33:41 PM
No, soy ganador.  Or is it soy ganadora.  Or estoy ganadora??

Estoy ganando. Igoogle says this one means "I am gaining."

Am I gaining or am I losing?

"Ganador" would refer to a male while female would be "ganadora".  The translation has a specific meaning depending on the sentence structure.  "Ganando" would really mean winning and "gano" is to have won as in past tense. When you "gain" it takes a bit of a twist and could mean to receive or increase and would be from the verbs "recibir" or "subio".  Anyway, bottom line is you got it wrong dear.  You put a coma after "No, soy ganador / a".  When you put the come you mistakenly disagreed with my statement and you basically stated that "NO" you are not a loser but a winner and of course we all know that to be false. What you meant to say was "No soy ganadora!".  Which could also be written "Yo soy la perdedora" or I am the loser (perdedora meaning a female loser)


Please exit to your left...Thank You!

(http://www1.istockphoto.com/file_thumbview_approve/245824/2/istockphoto_245824_winner_and_loser)


This has been another public service by NYC NATIVE!

Jackson Hts News:    So, what happen to you Castillo?

Castillo:  What yoo meen?

Jackson Hts News:  Well, the A-rod pop-up!  You dropped it.

Castillo:  Don't yoo want to talk 'bout sonesing else?

Jackson Hts News:  I'm sorry Luis, people want to know what happened?

Castillo:  Do yoo know me was National League Gold Glove tree time? 

Jackson Hts News:  Luis, what crossed your mind when you dropped the ball giving the Yankees the 9 - 8 win on the 9Th inning.

Castillo:  The sun hit me I.  Me no si the ball very good.

Jackson Hts News:  Umm, it was evening Luis.  The sun couldn't have possibly interfered with your visibility.

Castillo:  Why yoo say big words to mi.  White peepol very bad.  Me no entiendo but that don mean I am estupid!

Jackson Hts News:  Sorry, we didn't mean to offend you Luis.  What we meant to say was that the sun had already set and it could not bother your eyes at the time you were playing.  So, what happened Luis?

Castillo:  Vete pa' el infierno, maldito gringo.  Si te cojo en la calle te esploto cabeza de repollo.  O!
 
Jackson Hts News:  (Turning away to the camera confused but smiling) So, there you have it!  Luis Castillo's cabeza de repollo..or something like that is what really happened.

Here is an insert of an email I received.  Finally, someone is doing something about the abuse (mainly Chase) in forcing prices down.  I discourage anyone trying to sell an apartment or property from allowing the buyer to use Chase as their lender.  They are actually taking a totally fair market sale and forcing it down 5% to 10% putting the seller in a position of disadvantage.  Lucky for me our sponsors aren't taking it and are simply saying NO.  If you want a fair appraisal's go to Wells Fargo or Band Of America.  HSBC will turn down the deal if there is any kind of law suits (even a simple slip and fall) and TD Bank just started doing their own loans so I don't know where thky are going with it.  Sellers, BEWARE!!!  Find out who the buyer is using before accepting their offer.  Explain to them what is happening and if they insist in using them make sure there is a clause in your contract that obligates them to use your preferred lender if theirs turn the loan down or under appraises the property.  I'm not talking about obvious over price properties like many you saw in the new constrcution in Corona, Jamaica, elmhurst etc even in some parts of Jackson Heights.  I'm talking about logically well priced properties that otherwise appraise fairly within the area. 

Emal sent today
To:      All REALTORSÂ®

From: Charles McMillan, 2009 NAR President

Re:     Appraisals

Dear Fellow REALTORÂ®,

During the past two months, we have heard from many of you regarding problems with appraisals that are causing deals to be delayed or canceled altogether. I assure you that we on the NAR Leadership Team are experiencing the same problems in our businesses. In fact, VP & Liaison to Committees Steve Brown recently shared his experiences in Ohio on the Voices of Real Estate blog.
http://narblog1.realtors.org/mvtype/president/2009/06/all_is_not_quiet_on_the_midwes.html (http://narblog1.realtors.org/mvtype/president/2009/06/all_is_not_quiet_on_the_midwes.html)

Let me update you on what NAR is doing to resolve these problems quickly.

On Monday, June 29th, I will be in New York to meet with the Deputy Attorney General and his staff who worked directly on the Home Valuation Code of Conduct. I plan to share our concerns, as well as your stories, and ask for their assistance in resolving any problems related to the HVCC.

On Tuesday, June 30th, I will travel to Washington, D.C., to meet with the Director of the Federal Housing Finance Agency to discuss ways we can work with Fannie Mae, Freddie Mac and lenders to ensure that appraisals are accurate.

We will keep you posted on the outcome of these meetings. In the meantime, I encourage you to check out the following resources on Realtor.org for more information on the HVCC and how appraisal problems are impacting the real estate market:

Economists Podcast
http://www.realtor.org/research/research/research_podcast062309?LID=RONav0021  (http://www.realtor.org/research/research/research_podcast062309?LID=RONav0021)

HVCC
http://www.realtor.org/government_affairs/gapublic/gses_hvcc_announced  (http://www.realtor.org/government_affairs/gapublic/gses_hvcc_announced)

Appraisal Blog
http://narblog1.realtors.org/mvtype/appraisalinsight/  (http://narblog1.realtors.org/mvtype/appraisalinsight/)

On behalf of the entire Leadership Team and staff, I thank all of you who have shared your experiences and concerns with us. With your continued participation, I believe we will overcome this challenge in much the same way as we have conquered others â€“ "United Toward Tomorrow."

Sincerely,



Charles McMillan
CIPS, GRI

Title: Re: The Last Word!
Post by: NYC Native on March 22, 2010, 10:56:06 PM
Well. I ordered a cake for my youngest son's Birthday at Nitin by Roosevelt on the Elmhurst side.  It was a Dominican B'day Cake so In my opinion it can be hit and miss.  I was very happy with the cake, it was beautiful and very delicious.  The larger square cake was made with Dulce de leche filling and the smaller round cakes were made with fresh strawberries.  For those not familiar with Dominican cakes it is made with a sudo traditional french sponge cake.  I have eaten it many times and personally feel most of them are over rated but when it is done correctly it can be some of the most delicious Birthday cakes You can get.  So, two thumbs up Nitin for making a great Bday at a very affordable price...
(http://photos-e.ak.fbcdn.net/hphotos-ak-snc3/hs478.snc3/26178_404868338273_729198273_4881064_1172419_n.jpg)

Title: Re: The Last Word!
Post by: Beech Court on July 02, 2010, 12:04:33 AM
What is the absolute last word in any dictionary?

Zyxt is listed as the last word in the online Oxford English Dictionary, an obsolete Kentish word that is the second singular indicative present form of the verb see. The next-to-last is zyxst, an obsolete word meaning 'sixth'. Several online dictionaries list the word zyzzyva, a tropical American weevil, as the last word in the letter Z.

 ;D  ;D  ;D

(taken from Dictionary.com)

Title: Re: The Last Word!
Post by: Beech Court on August 03, 2011, 11:10:14 PM
Quote from: madalyn on August 03, 2011, 10:00:30 PM
I guess there are lots of different kinds of weevils.  Wonder who gave zyzzyvas such a cute name.....

The weevil is no longer than an ant. It was first discovered in 1922 in Brazil, and named by  Thomas Lincoln Casey, Jr. An entomologist at New York's Museum of Natural History thought that, because there was not a Latin name or Brazilian name associated with this weevil, it was probably named Zyzzyva as a practical joke to place it in a prominent ending position in many guides and manuals.
